	<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">Caroline Kennedy</h1>
	
	<div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">
		<div id="siteSub" class="noprint">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
		<div id="contentSub"></div>
		
		
		
		<div id="jump-to-nav"></div>
		<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#mw-head">Jump to navigation</a>
		<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#p-search">Jump to search</a>
		<div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><div class="mw-parser-output"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">This article is about President John F. Kennedy's daughter. For John F. Kennedy Jr.'s wife, see <a href="/wiki/Carolyn_Bessette-Kennedy" title="Carolyn Bessette-Kennedy">Carolyn Bessette-Kennedy</a>.</div>
<div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">American author and diplomat</div>
<p class="mw-empty-elt">
</p>
<table class="infobox vcard" style="width:22em"><tbody><tr><th colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-size:125%;font-weight:bold;font-size: 100%;"><div style="display:inline-block; font-size:130%;" Hyland</td></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="text-align:left"><span class="nowrap">Preceded by</span></th><td><a href="/wiki/John_Roos" title="John Roos">John Roos</a></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" </td></tr><tr><th colspan="2" style="text-align:center;background:lavender">Personal details</th></tr><tr><th scope="row">Born</th><td><div style="display:inline" class="nickname">Caroline Bouvier Kennedy</div><br /><span style="display:none"> (<span class="bday">1957-11-27</span>) </span>November 27, 1957<span class="noprint ForceAgeToShow"> (age&#160;61)</span><br /><a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York City</a>, <a href="/wiki/New_York_(state)" title="New York (state)">New York</a>, U.S.</td></tr><tr><th scope="row">Political party</th><td><a href="/wiki/Democratic_Party_(United_States)" title="Democratic Party (United States)">Democratic</a></td></tr><tr><th scope="row">Spouse(s)</th><td><div style="display:inline-block;line-height:normal;margin:2px 0px;"><a href="/wiki/Edwin_Schlossberg" title="Edwin Schlossberg">Edwin Schlossberg</a>&#32;&#40;<abbr title="married">m.</abbr>&#160;<span title="July 19, 1986">1986</span>&#41;</div></td></tr><tr><th scope="row">Children</th><td><div class="hlist hlist-separated"><ul><li><a href="/wiki/Rose_Schlossberg" title="Rose Schlossberg">Rose</a></li><li><a href="/wiki/Tatiana_Schlossberg" title="Tatiana Schlossberg">Tatiana</a></li><li><a href="/wiki/Jack_Schlossberg" title="Jack Schlossberg">Jack</a></li></ul></div></td></tr><tr><th scope="row">Parents</th><td><div class="plainlist">
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/John_F._Kennedy" title="John F. Kennedy">John F. Kennedy</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Jacqueline_Kennedy_Onassis" title="Jacqueline Kennedy Onassis">Jacqueline Kennedy Onassis</a></li></ul>
</div></td></tr><tr><th scope="row">Relatives</th><td>See <a href="/wiki/Kennedy_family" title="Kennedy family">Kennedy family</a></td></tr><tr><th scope="row">Education</th><td><a href="/wiki/Harvard_University" title="Harvard University">Harvard University</a> (<a href="/wiki/Bachelor_of_Arts" title="Bachelor of Arts">BA</a>)<br /><a href="/wiki/Columbia_University" title="Columbia University">Columbia University</a> (<a href="/wiki/Juris_Doctor" title="Juris Doctor">JD</a>)</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p><b>Caroline Bouvier Kennedy</b><sup id="cite_ref-no_name_change_1-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-no_name_change-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Larry_King_name_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Larry_King_name-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> (born November 27, 1957)<sup id="cite_ref-JFKLibrary_profile_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JFKLibrary_profile-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> is an American author, attorney, and diplomat who served as the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Ambassador_to_Japan" class="mw-redirect" title="United States Ambassador to Japan">United States Ambassador to Japan</a> from 2013 to 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> She is a prominent member of the <a href="/wiki/Kennedy_family" title="Kennedy family">Kennedy family</a> and the only surviving child of <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_United_States" title="President of the United States">President</a> <a href="/wiki/John_F._Kennedy" title="John F. Kennedy">John F. Kennedy</a> and <a href="/wiki/First_Lady_of_the_United_States" title="First Lady of the United States">First Lady</a> <a href="/wiki/Jacqueline_Kennedy_Onassis" title="Jacqueline Kennedy Onassis">Jacqueline Bouvier Kennedy</a>.
</p><p>Kennedy was five days shy of her sixth birthday when <a href="/wiki/Assassination_of_John_F._Kennedy" title="Assassination of John F. Kennedy">her father was assassinated</a> on November 22, 1963. The following year, Caroline, her mother, and brother <a href="/wiki/John_F._Kennedy_Jr." title="John F. Kennedy Jr.">John F. Kennedy Jr.</a> settled on the <a href="/wiki/Upper_East_Side" title="Upper East Side">Upper East Side</a> of <a href="/wiki/Manhattan" title="Manhattan">Manhattan</a>, where she attended school. Kennedy graduated from <a href="/wiki/Radcliffe_College" title="Radcliffe College">Radcliffe College</a> and worked at Manhattan's <a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_Museum_of_Art" title="Metropolitan Museum of Art">Metropolitan Museum of Art</a>, where she met her future husband, exhibit designer <a href="/wiki/Edwin_Schlossberg" title="Edwin Schlossberg">Edwin Schlossberg</a>. She went on to receive a <a href="/wiki/Juris_Doctor" title="Juris Doctor">J.D.</a> degree from <a href="/wiki/Columbia_Law_School" title="Columbia Law School">Columbia Law School</a>. Most of Kennedy's professional life has spanned law and politics, as well as education reform and charitable work. She has also acted as a spokesperson for her family's legacy and co-authored <a href="#Works_published">two books</a> with Ellen Aldermanon on <a href="/wiki/Civil_liberties" title="Civil liberties">civil liberties</a>.
</p><p>Early in the primary race for the <a href="/wiki/2008_United_States_presidential_election" title="2008 United States presidential election">2008 presidential election</a>, Kennedy and her uncle Ted endorsed Democratic candidate <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Barack Obama</a>; she later <a href="/wiki/Stump_speech_(politics)" title="Stump speech (politics)">stumped</a> for him in Florida, Indiana, and Ohio, served as co-chair of his <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Party_(United_States)_vice_presidential_candidates,_2008" class="mw-redirect" title="Democratic Party (United States) vice presidential candidates, 2008">Vice Presidential Search Committee</a>, and addressed the <a href="/wiki/2008_Democratic_National_Convention" title="2008 Democratic National Convention">2008 Democratic National Convention</a> in <a href="/wiki/Denver" title="Denver">Denver</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>After Obama selected United States Senator <a href="/wiki/Hillary_Clinton" title="Hillary Clinton">Hillary Clinton</a> to serve as <a href="/wiki/United_States_Secretary_of_State" title="United States Secretary of State">Secretary of State</a>, Kennedy expressed interest in being appointed to Clinton's vacant Senate seat from New York, but she later withdrew from consideration, citing "personal reasons." Congresswoman <a href="/wiki/Kirsten_Gillibrand" title="Kirsten Gillibrand">Kirsten Gillibrand</a> ultimately replaced Clinton as the junior New York Senator. In 2013, President Obama appointed Kennedy as the United States Ambassador to Japan.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_life">Early life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Caroline_Kennedy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Early life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="White_House_years">White House years</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Caroline_Kennedy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: White House years">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:JFK_with_Caroline_on_the_Honey_Fitz,_1963.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/JFK_with_Caroline_on_the_Honey_Fitz%2C_1963.jpg/220px-JFK_with_Caroline_on_the_Honey_Fitz%2C_1963.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="145" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/JFK_with_Caroline_on_the_Honey_Fitz%2C_1963.jpg/330px-JFK_with_Caroline_on_the_Honey_Fitz%2C_1963.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/JFK_with_Caroline_on_the_Honey_Fitz%2C_1963.jpg/440px-JFK_with_Caroline_on_the_Honey_Fitz%2C_1963.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2525" data-file-height="1667" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:JFK_with_Caroline_on_the_Honey_Fitz,_1963.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Caroline with her father aboard the yacht <i>Honey Fitz</i> off the coast of <a href="/wiki/Hyannis,_Massachusetts" title="Hyannis, Massachusetts">Hyannis, Massachusetts</a> at age five, August 25, 1963.</div></div></div>
<p>Caroline Bouvier Kennedy was born on November 27, 1957, at <a href="/wiki/Cornell_Medical_Center" class="mw-redirect" title="Cornell Medical Center">Cornell Medical Center</a> in <a href="/wiki/Manhattan" title="Manhattan">Manhattan</a> to <a href="/wiki/John_F._Kennedy" title="John F. Kennedy">John Fitzgerald Kennedy</a> (United States Senator from <a href="/wiki/Massachusetts" title="Massachusetts">Massachusetts</a>) and <a href="/wiki/Jacqueline_Kennedy_Onassis" title="Jacqueline Kennedy Onassis">Jacqueline Lee Bouvier Kennedy</a>. Caroline is named after her maternal aunt, <a href="/wiki/Lee_Radziwill" title="Lee Radziwill">Lee Radziwill</a>. A year before Caroline's birth, her parents had a stillborn daughter named Arabella. Caroline had a younger brother, <a href="/wiki/John_F._Kennedy_Jr." title="John F. Kennedy Jr.">John Jr.</a>, who was born just before her third birthday in 1960. Her infant brother, <a href="/wiki/Patrick_Bouvier_Kennedy" title="Patrick Bouvier Kennedy">Patrick</a>, died two days after his premature birth in 1963. Caroline lived with her parents in <a href="/wiki/Georgetown,_Washington,_D.C." class="mw-redirect" title="Georgetown, Washington, D.C.">Georgetown, Washington, D.C.</a> during the first three years of her life.<sup id="cite_ref-Georgetown_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Georgetown-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> When Caroline was three years old, the family moved to the <a href="/wiki/White_House" title="White House">White House</a> after her father <a href="/wiki/Inauguration_of_John_F._Kennedy" title="Inauguration of John F. Kennedy">was sworn in as President of the United States</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Georgetown_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Georgetown-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Caroline frequently attended kindergarten in classes that were organized by her mother, and she was often photographed riding her pony "Macaroni" around the White House grounds. One such photo in a news article inspired singer-songwriter <a href="/wiki/Neil_Diamond" title="Neil Diamond">Neil Diamond</a> to write his <a href="/wiki/Top_40" title="Top 40">Top Ten</a> hit song, "<a href="/wiki/Sweet_Caroline" title="Sweet Caroline">Sweet Caroline</a>", which he revealed when he performed it for Caroline's 50th birthday.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> As a small child, Caroline received numerous gifts from dignitaries, including a puppy from <a href="/wiki/Premier_of_the_Soviet_Union" title="Premier of the Soviet Union">Soviet Premier</a> <a href="/wiki/Nikita_Khrushchev" title="Nikita Khrushchev">Nikita Khrushchev</a> and a Yucatán pony from <a href="/wiki/Vice_President_of_the_United_States" title="Vice President of the United States">Vice President</a> <a href="/wiki/Lyndon_B._Johnson" title="Lyndon B. Johnson">Lyndon B. Johnson</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> Historians described Caroline's childhood personality as "a trifle remote and a bit shy at times" yet "remarkably unspoiled."<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> "She's too young to realize all these luxuries", her paternal grandmother, <a href="/wiki/Rose_Kennedy" title="Rose Kennedy">Rose Kennedy</a>, said of her. "She probably thinks it's natural for children to go off in their own airplanes. But she is with her cousins, and some of them dance and swim better than she. They do not allow her to take special precedence. Little children accept things".<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On the day of <a href="/wiki/Assassination_of_John_F._Kennedy" title="Assassination of John F. Kennedy">JFK's assassination</a> on November 22, 1963, nanny Maud Shaw took Caroline and John Jr. away from the White House to the home of their maternal grandmother, <a href="/wiki/Janet_Lee_Bouvier" title="Janet Lee Bouvier">Janet Bouvier Auchincloss</a>, who insisted that Shaw would be the one to tell Caroline about her father's assassination. That evening, Caroline and John Jr. returned to the White House, and while Caroline was sleeping in her bed, Shaw broke the news to her.<sup id="cite_ref-Heymann110-114_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Heymann110-114-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> Shaw soon found out that Jacqueline had wanted to be the one to tell the two children; this caused a rift between the nanny and Jacqueline.<sup id="cite_ref-Heymann110-114_12-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Heymann110-114-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> On December 6, two weeks after the assassination, Jacqueline, Caroline, and John Jr. moved out of the White House and returned to Georgetown.<sup id="cite_ref-nyt12071963_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nyt12071963-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> However, their new home soon became a popular tourist attraction. They left Georgetown the following year and later moved to a penthouse apartment at <a href="/wiki/1040_Fifth_Avenue" title="1040 Fifth Avenue">1040 Fifth Avenue</a> on the <a href="/wiki/Upper_East_Side" title="Upper East Side">Upper East Side of Manhattan</a> in <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York City</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Georgetown_7-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Georgetown-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Later_childhood_years">Later childhood years</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Caroline_Kennedy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Later childhood years">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 1967, Caroline christened the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Navy" title="United States Navy">U.S. Navy</a> <a href="/wiki/Aircraft_carrier" title="Aircraft carrier">aircraft carrier</a> <a href="/wiki/USS_John_F._Kennedy_(CV-67)" title="USS John F. Kennedy (CV-67)">USS <i>John F. Kennedy</i></a> in a widely publicized ceremony in <a href="/wiki/Newport_News,_Virginia" title="Newport News, Virginia">Newport News, Virginia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Over that summer, Jacqueline took the children on a six-week "sentimental journey"<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Inline_citation#When_you_must_use_inline_citations" title="Wikipedia:Inline citation"><span title="The text near this tag needs a citation. (March 2018)">This quote needs a citation</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> to Ireland, where they met <a href="/wiki/President_of_Ireland" title="President of Ireland">President</a> <a href="/wiki/%C3%89amon_de_Valera" title="Éamon de Valera">Éamon de Valera</a> and visited the Kennedy ancestral home at Dunganstown. In the midst of the trip, Caroline and John were surrounded by a large number of press photographers while playing in a pond. The incident caused their mother to telephone Ireland's Department of External Affairs and request the issuing of a statement that she and the children wanted to be left in peace. As a result of the request, further attempts by press photographers to photograph the threesome ended with arrests by local police and the photographers being jailed.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Uncle <a href="/wiki/Robert_F._Kennedy" title="Robert F. Kennedy">Robert F. Kennedy</a> became a major presence in the lives of Caroline and John following their father's assassination, and Caroline saw him as a surrogate father. When Bobby <a href="/wiki/Assassination_of_Robert_F._Kennedy" title="Assassination of Robert F. Kennedy">was assassinated</a> in June 1968, Jacqueline sought a means of protecting them, stating: "If they're killing Kennedys, then my children are targets ... I want to get out of this country".<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> Jacqueline Kennedy married Greek shipping tycoon <a href="/wiki/Aristotle_Onassis" title="Aristotle Onassis">Aristotle Onassis</a> several months later and she and the children moved to <a href="/wiki/Skorpios" title="Skorpios">Skorpios</a>, his Greek island. The next year, 11-year-old Caroline attended the funeral of her grandfather, <a href="/wiki/Joseph_P._Kennedy,_Sr." class="mw-redirect" title="Joseph P. Kennedy, Sr.">Joseph P. Kennedy, Sr.</a> Her cousin, David, asked her about her feelings towards her mother's new husband and she replied, "I don't like him".<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1970, Jacqueline wrote her brother-in-law <a href="/wiki/Ted_Kennedy" title="Ted Kennedy">Ted Kennedy</a> a letter stating that Caroline had been without a godfather since Bobby's death and would like him to assume the role. Ted began making regular trips from Washington to New York to see Caroline, where she was in school.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> In 1971, Caroline returned to the White House for the first time since her father's assassination when she was invited by President <a href="/wiki/Richard_Nixon" title="Richard Nixon">Richard Nixon</a> to view the official portrait of her father.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Onassis died in March 1975, and Caroline returned to Skorpios for his funeral. A few days later she and her mother and brother attended the presentation by <a href="/wiki/President_of_France" title="President of France">French president</a> <a href="/wiki/Val%C3%A9ry_Giscard_d%27Estaing" title="Valéry Giscard d&#39;Estaing">Valéry Giscard d'Estaing</a> of the Legion of Honor award to her aunt, <a href="/wiki/Eunice_Kennedy_Shriver" title="Eunice Kennedy Shriver">Eunice Kennedy Shriver</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> Later that year, Caroline was visiting <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a> to complete a year-long art course at the <a href="/wiki/Sotheby%27s" title="Sotheby&#39;s">Sotheby's</a> auction house, when an IRA car bomb placed under the car of her hosts, Conservative MP <a href="/wiki/Hugh_Fraser_(British_politician)" title="Hugh Fraser (British politician)">Sir Hugh Fraser</a> and his wife, <a href="/wiki/Antonia_Fraser" title="Antonia Fraser">Antonia</a>, exploded shortly before she and the Frasers were due to leave for their daily drive to Sotheby's. Caroline had not yet left the house, but a neighbor, oncologist Professor <a href="/wiki/Gordon_Hamilton_Fairley" title="Gordon Hamilton Fairley">Gordon Hamilton Fairley</a>, was passing by when he was walking his dog and was killed by the explosion.<sup id="cite_ref-bomb_kills_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bomb_kills-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education_and_personal_life">Education and personal life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Caroline_Kennedy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Education and personal life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Kennedy attended <a href="/wiki/The_Brearley_School" class="mw-redirect" title="The Brearley School">The Brearley School</a> and <a href="/wiki/Convent_of_the_Sacred_Heart_(New_York)" class="mw-redirect" title="Convent of the Sacred Heart (New York)">Convent of the Sacred Heart</a> in New York City and graduated from <a href="/wiki/Concord_Academy" title="Concord Academy">Concord Academy</a> in Massachusetts in 1975.<sup id="cite_ref-Heymann,_p._203_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Heymann,_p._203-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup>  She was a photographer's assistant at the <a href="/wiki/1976_Winter_Olympics" title="1976 Winter Olympics">1976 Winter Olympics</a> in <a href="/wiki/Innsbruck" title="Innsbruck">Innsbruck</a>, Austria.<sup id="cite_ref-journalism_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-journalism-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> In 1977, she worked as a summer intern at the New York <i><a href="/wiki/Daily_News_(New_York)" class="mw-redirect" title="Daily News (New York)">Daily News</a></i>, earning $156 a week ($673.41 in 2019 dollars), "fetching coffee for harried editors and reporters, changing typewriter ribbons and delivering messages."<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> Kennedy reportedly "sat on a bench alone for two hours the first day before other employees even said hello to her"; and, according to Richard Licata, a former <i>News</i> reporter, "Everyone was too scared."<sup id="cite_ref-journalism_24-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-journalism-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup>  Kennedy also wrote for <i><a href="/wiki/Rolling_Stone" title="Rolling Stone">Rolling Stone</a></i> about visiting <a href="/wiki/Graceland" title="Graceland">Graceland</a> shortly after the death of <a href="/wiki/Elvis_Presley" title="Elvis Presley">Elvis Presley</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-journalism_24-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-journalism-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1980, she earned a <a href="/wiki/Bachelor_of_Arts" title="Bachelor of Arts">Bachelor of Arts</a> from <a href="/wiki/Radcliffe_College" title="Radcliffe College">Radcliffe College</a> at <a href="/wiki/Harvard_University" title="Harvard University">Harvard University</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-UPIphoto_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UPIphoto-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup>  During college, Kennedy had "considered becoming a photojournalist, but soon realized she could never make her living observing other people because they were too busy watching her."<sup id="cite_ref-journalism_24-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-journalism-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> After graduating, Kennedy was hired as a research assistant in the Film and Television Department of the <a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_Museum_of_Art" title="Metropolitan Museum of Art">Metropolitan Museum of Art</a> in New York. She later became a "liaison officer between the museum staff and outside producers and directors shooting footage at the museum", helping coordinate the <i><a href="/wiki/Sesame_Street" title="Sesame Street">Sesame Street</a></i> special <i><a href="/wiki/Don%27t_Eat_the_Pictures_(special)" class="mw-redirect" title="Don&#39;t Eat the Pictures (special)">Don't Eat the Pictures</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> On December 4, 1984, Caroline was threatened when a man telephoned the museum and stated his name and address while reporting that a bomb had been planted there. Three days later, he was arrested for the threat.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> In 1988, she earned a <a href="/wiki/Juris_Doctor" title="Juris Doctor">Juris Doctor</a> from <a href="/wiki/Columbia_Law_School" title="Columbia Law School">Columbia Law School</a>, graduating in the top ten percent of her class.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>While working at the Met, Kennedy met her future husband, exhibit designer <a href="/wiki/Edwin_Schlossberg" title="Edwin Schlossberg">Edwin Schlossberg</a>. They married in 1986 at Our Lady of Victory Church in <a href="/wiki/Centerville,_Massachusetts" title="Centerville, Massachusetts">Centerville, Massachusetts</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-NYT_19860302_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYT_19860302-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> Kennedy's first cousin <a href="/wiki/Maria_Shriver" title="Maria Shriver">Maria Shriver</a> served as the bride's matron of honor, and Ted later walked her down the aisle. Kennedy is sometimes incorrectly referred to  as "Caroline Kennedy Schlossberg", but she did not change her name at the time she married.<sup id="cite_ref-no_name_change_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-no_name_change-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Larry_King_name_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Larry_King_name-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> Kennedy has three children: <a href="/wiki/Rose_Schlossberg" title="Rose Schlossberg">Rose Kennedy Schlossberg</a> (born 1988), <a href="/wiki/Tatiana_Schlossberg" title="Tatiana Schlossberg">Tatiana Celia Kennedy Schlossberg</a> (born 1990), and <a href="/wiki/Jack_Schlossberg" title="Jack Schlossberg">John Bouvier Kennedy Schlossberg</a>, known as Jack (born 1993).
</p><p>Raised in Manhattan and somewhat separated from their Hyannisport cousins,<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> Caroline and John Jr. were very close, and especially so following their mother's death in 1994.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> After John Jr. <a href="/wiki/John_F._Kennedy_Jr._plane_crash" title="John F. Kennedy Jr. plane crash">died in a plane crash</a> in 1999, Caroline was the only remaining survivor of the former President's immediate family, and she preferred not to have a public memorial service for her brother.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> She decided that his remains would be cremated and his ashes scattered into the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Ocean" title="Atlantic Ocean">Atlantic Ocean</a> off the coast of <a href="/wiki/Martha%27s_Vineyard" title="Martha&#39;s Vineyard">Martha's Vineyard</a>, where he met his fate.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> John Jr. bequeathed Caroline his half ownership of <i><a href="/wiki/George_(magazine)" title="George (magazine)">George</a></i> magazine, but Caroline believed that her brother would not have wanted the magazine to continue following his death,<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> and the magazine ceased publication two years later.<sup id="cite_ref-cnn_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cnn-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Kennedy owns her mother's 375-acre (152&#160;ha) estate known as Red Gate Farm in <a href="/wiki/Aquinnah,_Massachusetts" title="Aquinnah, Massachusetts">Aquinnah</a> (formerly Gay Head) on <a href="/wiki/Martha%27s_Vineyard" title="Martha&#39;s Vineyard">Martha's Vineyard</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-NYT-JKO_obit_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYT-JKO_obit-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> The New York <i>Daily News</i> estimated Kennedy's net worth in 2008 at over $100 million.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> During her 2013 nomination to serve as Ambassador to Japan, financial disclosure reports showed her net worth to be between $67 million and $278 million, including family trusts, government and public authority bonds, commercial property in New York, Chicago and Washington, and holdings in the Cayman Islands.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span id="Public_career:_1989.E2.80.93present"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Public_career:_1989–present">Public career: 1989–present</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Caroline_Kennedy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Public career: 1989–present">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 210px; float: right; clear: right; margin:0 0 1.5em 1.5em"><caption>External video</caption><tbody><tr><td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;text-align: left"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Nuvola_apps_kaboodle.svg/16px-Nuvola_apps_kaboodle.svg.png" decoding="async" width="16" height="16" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Nuvola_apps_kaboodle.svg/24px-Nuvola_apps_kaboodle.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Nuvola_apps_kaboodle.svg/32px-Nuvola_apps_kaboodle.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="128" data-file-height="128" /> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.c-span.org/video/?17736-1/defense-bill-rights-action"><i>Booknotes</i> interview with Ellen Alderman and Caroline Kennedy on <i>In Our Defense</i>, April 28, 1991</a>, <a href="/wiki/C-SPAN" title="C-SPAN">C-SPAN</a></td></tr></tbody></table>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Caroline_Kennedy_1999.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Caroline_Kennedy_1999.jpg/170px-Caroline_Kennedy_1999.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="275" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Caroline_Kennedy_1999.jpg/255px-Caroline_Kennedy_1999.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Caroline_Kennedy_1999.jpg/340px-Caroline_Kennedy_1999.jpg 2x" data-file-width="871" data-file-height="1408" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Caroline_Kennedy_1999.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Kennedy in 1999</div></div></div>
<p>Kennedy is an attorney, writer, and editor who has served on the boards of numerous non-profit organizations. She wrote the book, "In Our Defense: The Bill of Rights In Action" in collaboration with Ellen Alderman, which was published in 1991. During an interview regarding the volume, Caroline explained that the two wanted to show why the <a href="/wiki/Fourth_Amendment_of_the_United_States_Constitution" class="mw-redirect" title="Fourth Amendment of the United States Constitution">Fourth Amendment of the United States Constitution</a> was written.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> She attended the Robin Hood Foundation annual breakfast on December 7, 1999. Her brother John had been committed to the organization, which Caroline spoke of at the event.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> In 2000, she supported <a href="/wiki/Al_Gore" title="Al Gore">Al Gore</a> for the presidency and mentioned feeling a kinship with him since their fathers served together in the Senate.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup>  Kennedy spoke at the <a href="/wiki/2000_Democratic_National_Convention" title="2000 Democratic National Convention">2000 Democratic National Convention</a> which was held in <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles" title="Los Angeles">Los Angeles</a>, California, the first time since the <a href="/wiki/1960_Democratic_National_Convention" title="1960 Democratic National Convention">1960 Democratic National Convention</a>, where her father had been nominated by the Democratic Party for the presidency.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>From 2002 through 2004, she worked as director of the Office of Strategic Partnerships for the <a href="/wiki/New_York_City_Department_of_Education" title="New York City Department of Education">New York City Department of Education</a>, appointed by School Chancellor Joel Klein. The three-day-a-week job paid her a salary of $1 and had the goal of raising private money for the New York City public schools;<sup id="cite_ref-NYCschooljob_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYCschooljob-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> she helped raise more than $65 million.<sup id="cite_ref-JFKLibrary_profile_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JFKLibrary_profile-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-leaving_45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-leaving-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> She served as one of two vice chairs of the board of directors of The Fund for Public Schools and is currently Honorary Director of the Fund.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> She has also served on the board of trustees of Concord Academy, which she attended as a teen.<sup id="cite_ref-Heymann,_p._203_23-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Heymann,_p._203-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Kennedy and other members of her family created the <a href="/wiki/Profile_in_Courage_Award" title="Profile in Courage Award">Profile in Courage Award</a> in 1989. The award is given to a public official or officials whose actions demonstrate politically courageous leadership in the spirit of John F. Kennedy's book, <i><a href="/wiki/Profiles_in_Courage" title="Profiles in Courage">Profiles in Courage</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup>  In 2001, she presented the award to former president <a href="/wiki/Gerald_Ford" title="Gerald Ford">Gerald Ford</a> for his controversial pardon of former president <a href="/wiki/Richard_M._Nixon" class="mw-redirect" title="Richard M. Nixon">Richard M. Nixon</a> almost 30 years prior.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> She is also president of the <a href="/wiki/John_F._Kennedy_Library" class="mw-redirect" title="John F. Kennedy Library">Kennedy Library Foundation</a><sup id="cite_ref-JFKLibrary_profile_3-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JFKLibrary_profile-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> and an adviser to the <a href="/wiki/Harvard_Institute_of_Politics" title="Harvard Institute of Politics">Harvard Institute of Politics</a>, a living memorial to her father. Kennedy is a member of the New York and Washington, D.C., <a href="/wiki/Bar_association" title="Bar association">bar associations</a>. She is also a member of the boards of directors of the <a href="/wiki/Commission_on_Presidential_Debates" title="Commission on Presidential Debates">Commission on Presidential Debates</a> and the <a href="/wiki/NAACP_Legal_Defense_and_Educational_Fund" title="NAACP Legal Defense and Educational Fund">NAACP Legal Defense and Educational Fund</a>, and is an honorary chair of the <a href="/wiki/American_Ballet_Theatre" title="American Ballet Theatre">American Ballet Theatre</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> Kennedy represented her family at the funeral services of former presidents <a href="/wiki/Death_and_state_funeral_of_Ronald_Reagan" title="Death and state funeral of Ronald Reagan">Ronald Reagan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Death_and_state_funeral_of_Gerald_Ford" title="Death and state funeral of Gerald Ford">Gerald Ford</a> and former First Ladies <a href="/wiki/Lady_Bird_Johnson" title="Lady Bird Johnson">Lady Bird Johnson</a> and <a href="/wiki/Barbara_Bush" title="Barbara Bush">Barbara</a> <a href="/wiki/Barbara_Bush" title="Barbara Bush">Bush</a>. She also represented her family at the dedication of the <a href="/wiki/William_J._Clinton_Presidential_Center_and_Park" class="mw-redirect" title="William J. Clinton Presidential Center and Park">Bill Clinton Presidential Center and Park</a> in <a href="/wiki/Little_Rock,_Arkansas" title="Little Rock, Arkansas">Little Rock, Arkansas</a>, in November 2004. Kennedy attended the fiftieth-anniversary ceremony of the <a href="/wiki/March_on_Washington" class="mw-redirect" title="March on Washington">March on Washington</a> on August 28, 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>After her post as ambassador to Japan ended, the <a href="/wiki/Boeing" title="Boeing">Boeing Company</a> elected her in August 2017 to serve on its board of directors.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2008_and_2012_presidential_elections">2008 and 2012 presidential elections</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Caroline_Kennedy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: 2008 and 2012 presidential elections">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r889293853/mw-parser-output/.tmulti">.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbinner{display:flex;flex-direction:column}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .theader{clear:both;font-weight:bold;text-align:center;align-self:center;background-color:transparent;width:100%}.mw-parser-output .tmulti 2x" data-file-width="3185" data-file-height="2122" /></a></div></div></div><div class="trow"><div class="thumbcaption" style="text-align:left;background-color:">Kennedy on the presidential campaign trail</div></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Caroline_Kennedy_DNC_2008.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Caroline_Kennedy_DNC_2008.jpg/220px-Caroline_Kennedy_DNC_2008.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="150" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Caroline_Kennedy_DNC_2008.jpg/330px-Caroline_Kennedy_DNC_2008.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Caroline_Kennedy_DNC_2008.jpg/440px-Caroline_Kennedy_DNC_2008.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3644" data-file-height="2480" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Caroline_Kennedy_DNC_2008.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Kennedy spoke during the first night of the <a href="/wiki/2008_Democratic_National_Convention" title="2008 Democratic National Convention">2008 Democratic National Convention</a> in <a href="/wiki/Denver,_Colorado" class="mw-redirect" title="Denver, Colorado">Denver, Colorado</a>, on August 25, 2008, introducing her uncle, Senator <a href="/wiki/Ted_Kennedy" title="Ted Kennedy">Ted Kennedy</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>On January 27, 2008, Kennedy announced in a <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">New York Times</a></i> op-ed piece entitled, "A President Like My Father," that she would endorse <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Barack Obama</a> in the <a href="/wiki/2008_United_States_presidential_election" title="2008 United States presidential election">2008 U.S. presidential election</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-NYT_20080127_54-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYT_20080127-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> Her concluding lines were: "I have never had a president who inspired me the way people tell me that my father inspired them. But for the first time, I believe I have found the man who could be that president—not just for me, but for a new generation of Americans."<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Federal_Election_Commission" title="Federal Election Commission">Federal Election Commission</a> records show that Kennedy contributed $2,300 to the <a href="/wiki/Hillary_Clinton_presidential_campaign,_2008" class="mw-redirect" title="Hillary Clinton presidential campaign, 2008">Hillary Rodham Clinton presidential campaign committee</a> on June 29, 2007. She previously contributed a total of $5,000 to Clinton's 2006 senatorial campaign. On September 18, 2007, she contributed $2,300 to <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama_presidential_campaign,_2008" class="mw-redirect" title="Barack Obama presidential campaign, 2008">Barack Obama's presidential campaign committee</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-campaigndonations_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-campaigndonations-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On June 4, 2008, Obama named Kennedy, along with <a href="/wiki/James_A._Johnson_(businessman)" class="mw-redirect" title="James A. Johnson (businessman)">Jim Johnson</a> and <a href="/wiki/Eric_Holder" title="Eric Holder">Eric Holder</a>, to co-chair his Vice Presidential Search Committee.<sup id="cite_ref-FirstRead_Murray_20080604_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FirstRead_Murray_20080604-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> (Johnson withdrew one week later.) Filmmaker <a href="/wiki/Michael_Moore" title="Michael Moore">Michael Moore</a> called on Kennedy to "Pull a Cheney",<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> and name herself as Obama's vice presidential running mate (<a href="/wiki/Dick_Cheney" title="Dick Cheney">Dick Cheney</a> headed <a href="/wiki/George_W._Bush" title="George W. Bush">George W. Bush</a>'s vice presidential vetting committee in 2000—Cheney himself was chosen for the job<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup>). On August 23, Obama announced that Senator <a href="/wiki/Joe_Biden" title="Joe Biden">Joe Biden</a> of <a href="/wiki/Delaware" title="Delaware">Delaware</a> would be his running mate. Kennedy addressed the <a href="/wiki/2008_Democratic_National_Convention" title="2008 Democratic National Convention">2008 Democratic National Convention</a> in Denver, introducing a tribute film about her uncle, Senator Ted Kennedy.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Kennedy was among the 35 national co-chairs of Obama's 2012 re-election campaign.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup> On June 27, 2012, Kennedy made appearances in Nashua and Manchester, New Hampshire, to campaign for the re-election of President Obama.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>There has been media speculation that she is a possible candidate for the 2020 Presidential primaries and election.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="United_States_Senate_seat">United States Senate seat</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Caroline_Kennedy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: United States Senate seat">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/United_States_Senate_special_election_in_New_York,_2010#Potential_candidates" class="mw-redirect" title="United States Senate special election in New York, 2010">Possible appointment candidates for the New York Senate seat</a></div>
<p>In December 2008, Kennedy expressed interest in the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Senate" title="United States Senate">United States Senate</a> seat occupied by <a href="/wiki/Hillary_Clinton" title="Hillary Clinton">Hillary Clinton</a>, who had been selected to become <a href="/wiki/United_States_Secretary_of_State" title="United States Secretary of State">Secretary of State</a>. This seat was to be filled through 2010 by appointment of <a href="/wiki/List_of_Governors_of_New_York" class="mw-redirect" title="List of Governors of New York">New York Governor</a> <a href="/wiki/David_Paterson" title="David Paterson">David Paterson</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup> This same seat was held by Kennedy's uncle <a href="/wiki/Robert_F._Kennedy" title="Robert F. Kennedy">Robert F. Kennedy</a> from January 1965 until his <a href="/wiki/Assassination_of_Robert_F._Kennedy" title="Assassination of Robert F. Kennedy">assassination</a> in June 1968, when he was a candidate for the Democratic presidential nomination.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup> Kennedy's appointment was supported by Congresswoman <a href="/wiki/Louise_Slaughter" title="Louise Slaughter">Louise Slaughter</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> State Assemblyman <a href="/wiki/Vito_Lopez" class="mw-redirect" title="Vito Lopez">Vito Lopez</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-records_show_70-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-records_show-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> New York City mayor <a href="/wiki/Michael_Bloomberg" title="Michael Bloomberg">Michael Bloomberg</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup> former New York City Mayor <a href="/wiki/Ed_Koch" title="Ed Koch">Ed Koch</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-political_views_72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-political_views-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> and the <i><a href="/wiki/New_York_Post" title="New York Post">New York Post</a></i> editorial page.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>She was criticized for not voting in a number of Democratic primaries and general elections since registering in 1988 in New York City<sup id="cite_ref-records_show_70-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-records_show-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> and for not providing details about her political views.<sup id="cite_ref-political_views_72-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-political_views-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> In response, Kennedy released a statement through a spokeswoman that outlined some of her political views including that she supported legislation legalizing <a href="/wiki/Same-sex_marriage" title="Same-sex marriage">same-sex marriage</a>, was <a href="/wiki/Pro-choice" class="mw-redirect" title="Pro-choice">pro-choice</a>, against the death penalty, for restoring the <a href="/wiki/Federal_Assault_Weapons_Ban" title="Federal Assault Weapons Ban">Federal Assault Weapons Ban</a>, and believed the <a href="/wiki/North_American_Free_Trade_Agreement" title="North American Free Trade Agreement">North American Free Trade Agreement</a> (NAFTA) should be re-examined.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-NYT_political_views_75-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYT_political_views-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup>  On foreign policy, her spokeswoman reiterated that Kennedy opposed the Iraq War from the beginning as well as that she believed that <a href="/wiki/Jerusalem" title="Jerusalem">Jerusalem</a> should be the undivided capital city of <a href="/wiki/Israel" title="Israel">Israel</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup>  Kennedy declined to make disclosures of her financial dealings or other personal matters to the press, stating that she would not release the information publicly unless she were selected by Governor Paterson.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup> She did complete a confidential 28-page disclosure questionnaire required of hopefuls, reported to include extensive financial information.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>In an interview with the <a href="/wiki/Associated_Press" title="Associated Press">Associated Press</a>, Kennedy acknowledged that she would need to prove herself. "Going into politics is something people have asked me about forever", Kennedy said. "When this opportunity came along, which was sort of unexpected, I thought, 'Well, maybe now. How about now?' [I'll have to] work twice as hard as anybody else..... I am an unconventional choice..... We're starting to see there are many ways into public life and public service".<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup> In late December 2008, Kennedy drew criticism from several media outlets for lacking clarity in interviews, and for using the phrase "you know" 168 times during a 30-minute interview with <a href="/wiki/NY1" title="NY1">NY1</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Shortly before midnight on January 22, 2009, Kennedy released a statement that she was withdrawing from consideration for the seat, citing "personal reasons".<sup id="cite_ref-Times_81-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Times-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup> Kennedy declined to expand upon the reasons that led to her decision.<sup id="cite_ref-Times_81-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Times-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup> One day after Kennedy's withdrawal, Paterson announced his selection of Representative <a href="/wiki/Kirsten_Gillibrand" title="Kirsten Gillibrand">Kirsten Gillibrand</a> to fill the Senate seat.<sup id="cite_ref-withdrawal_statement_85-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-withdrawal_statement-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="United_States_Ambassador_to_Japan_.282013.E2.80.932017.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="United_States_Ambassador_to_Japan_(2013–2017)">United States Ambassador to Japan (2013–2017)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Caroline_Kennedy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: United States Ambassador to Japan (2013–2017)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Caroline_Kennedy_20131115.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Caroline_Kennedy_20131115.jpg/220px-Caroline_Kennedy_20131115.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Caroline_Kennedy_20131115.jpg/330px-Caroline_Kennedy_20131115.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Caroline_Kennedy_20131115.jpg/440px-Caroline_Kennedy_20131115.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3218" data-file-height="2142" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Caroline_Kennedy_20131115.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Kennedy makes her first statement after arriving at the <a href="/wiki/Narita_International_Airport" title="Narita International Airport">Narita International Airport</a> on November 15, 2013.</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ambassador_Kennedy_After_the_Presentation_of_Credentials_Ceremony_(10941227714).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Ambassador_Kennedy_After_the_Presentation_of_Credentials_Ceremony_%2810941227714%29.jpg/220px-Ambassador_Kennedy_After_the_Presentation_of_Credentials_Ceremony_%2810941227714%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Ambassador_Kennedy_After_the_Presentation_of_Credentials_Ceremony_%2810941227714%29.jpg/330px-Ambassador_Kennedy_After_the_Presentation_of_Credentials_Ceremony_%2810941227714%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Ambassador_Kennedy_After_the_Presentation_of_Credentials_Ceremony_%2810941227714%29.jpg/440px-Ambassador_Kennedy_After_the_Presentation_of_Credentials_Ceremony_%2810941227714%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4928" data-file-height="3280" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ambassador_Kennedy_After_the_Presentation_of_Credentials_Ceremony_(10941227714).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>In <a href="/wiki/Tokyo_Imperial_Palace" title="Tokyo Imperial Palace">Tokyo Imperial Palace</a></div></div></div>
<p>On July 24, 2013, President Obama announced Kennedy as his nominee to be <a href="/wiki/United_States_Ambassador_to_Japan" class="mw-redirect" title="United States Ambassador to Japan">United States Ambassador to Japan</a> to succeed Ambassador <a href="/wiki/John_Roos" title="John Roos">John Roos</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup>  The prospective nomination was first reported in February 2013<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup> and, in mid-July 2013, formal diplomatic agreement to the appointment was reportedly received from the Japanese government.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On September 19, 2013, Kennedy sat before the Senate Foreign Relations Committee and responded to questions from both Republican and Democratic senators regarding her potential appointment. Kennedy explained that her focus would be military ties, trade, and student exchange if she was selected for the position.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup>  She was confirmed in October by <a href="/wiki/Unanimous_consent" title="Unanimous consent">unanimous consent</a> as the first female U.S. Ambassador to Japan<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup> and was sworn in by <a href="/wiki/United_States_Secretary_of_State" title="United States Secretary of State">Secretary of State</a> <a href="/wiki/John_Kerry" title="John Kerry">John Kerry</a> on November 12.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup> Kennedy arrived in Japan on November 15<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup> and met Japanese diplomats three days later.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup> On November 19, <a href="/wiki/NHK" title="NHK">NHK</a> showed live coverage of Kennedy's arrival at the <a href="/wiki/Tokyo_Imperial_Palace" title="Tokyo Imperial Palace">Imperial Palace</a> to present her diplomatic credentials to <a href="/wiki/Emperor_Akihito" class="mw-redirect" title="Emperor Akihito">Emperor Akihito</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In December 2013, she visited <a href="/wiki/Nagasaki" title="Nagasaki">Nagasaki</a> to meet with survivors of the 1945 <a href="/wiki/Atomic_bombings_of_Hiroshima_and_Nagasaki" title="Atomic bombings of Hiroshima and Nagasaki">atomic bombing</a> of that city.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup>  On August 5, 2014, she attended a memorial ceremony for victims of the <a href="/wiki/Atomic_bombing_of_Hiroshima" class="mw-redirect" title="Atomic bombing of Hiroshima">atomic bombing of Hiroshima</a>; she was the second U.S. ambassador to attend the annual memorial. This was her second visit to Hiroshima, having visited in 1978 with her uncle, Senator Ted Kennedy.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In February 2014, Kennedy visited the southern Japanese island of Okinawa, the site of the large military bases of <a href="/wiki/United_States_Forces_Japan" title="United States Forces Japan">United States Forces Japan</a>, and was received by protests against the American military presence and placards with "no base" written on them. The protesters are opposed to the American military presence citing various concerns over sexual assaults and the environmental impact of the base.<sup id="cite_ref-GuardFeb_99-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GuardFeb-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup> Kennedy subsequently met with Okinawa's governor, <a href="/wiki/Hirokazu_Nakaima" title="Hirokazu Nakaima">Hirokazu Nakaima</a>, who was re-elected in 2010 in opposition to the base. She pledged to reduce the burden of the American military presence in Okinawa.<sup id="cite_ref-GuardFeb_99-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GuardFeb-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Caroline_Kennedy,_October_20,_2014.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Caroline_Kennedy%2C_October_20%2C_2014.jpg/220px-Caroline_Kennedy%2C_October_20%2C_2014.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="268" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Caroline_Kennedy%2C_October_20%2C_2014.jpg/330px-Caroline_Kennedy%2C_October_20%2C_2014.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Caroline_Kennedy%2C_October_20%2C_2014.jpg/440px-Caroline_Kennedy%2C_October_20%2C_2014.jpg 2x" data-file-width="668" data-file-height="815" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Caroline_Kennedy,_October_20,_2014.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Kennedy in October 2014</div></div></div>
<p>In April 2015, Kennedy visited the <a href="/wiki/Hiroshima_Peace_Memorial_Museum" title="Hiroshima Peace Memorial Museum">Hiroshima Peace Memorial Museum</a>, which displayed the impact from the 1945 atomic bombing. Kennedy called her visit a "solemn honor" and also planted dogwood trees on a road, participating in a U.S. project to spread 3,000 dogwood trees across Japan.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On August 6, 2015, Kennedy accompanied US <a href="/wiki/Under_Secretary_of_State_for_Arms_Control_and_International_Security_Affairs" title="Under Secretary of State for Arms Control and International Security Affairs">Under Secretary of State for Arms Control and International Security Affairs</a> <a href="/wiki/Rose_Gottemoeller" title="Rose Gottemoeller">Rose Gottemoeller</a> to the memorial for the <a href="/wiki/Atomic_bombings_of_Hiroshima_and_Nagasaki#Hiroshima" title="Atomic bombings of Hiroshima and Nagasaki">atomic bombing of Hiroshima, Japan</a> by the United States in World War II. It marked the 70th anniversary of the bombing, and Gottemoeller became the first senior American official to attend the annual memorial.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup> Kennedy was only the second US ambassador to attend. With representatives of 100 countries in attendance, Japanese <a href="/wiki/Prime_minister" title="Prime minister">prime minister</a> <a href="/wiki/Shinz%C5%8D_Abe" title="Shinzō Abe">Shinzō Abe</a> reiterated Japan's official support for the abolition of <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_weapons" class="mw-redirect" title="Nuclear weapons">nuclear weapons</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Kennedy resigned as the United States Ambassador to Japan shortly before Donald Trump was sworn in as the 45th President of the United States. She formally left Japan as Ambassador on January 18, 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Works_published">Works published</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Caroline_Kennedy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Works published">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Kennedy and Ellen Alderman have written two books together on civil liberties:
</p>
<ul><li><i>In Our Defense: The Bill of Rights In Action</i> (1991)<sup id="cite_ref-LoC_104-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LoC-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><i>The Right to Privacy</i> (1995)<sup id="cite_ref-LoC_104-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LoC-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>
<p>On her own, Kennedy has edited these <i>New York Times</i> best-selling volumes:
</p>
<ul><li><i>The Best-Loved Poems of Jacqueline Kennedy Onassis</i> (2001);<sup id="cite_ref-LoC_104-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LoC-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><i>Profiles in Courage for Our Time</i> (2002);<sup id="cite_ref-LoC_104-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LoC-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><i>A Patriot's Handbook</i> (2003);<sup id="cite_ref-LoC_104-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LoC-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><i>A Family of Poems: My Favorite Poetry for Children</i> (2005).<sup id="cite_ref-LoC_104-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LoC-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>
<p>She is also the author of <i>A Family Christmas</i>, a collection of poems, prose, and personal notes from her family history (2007, <style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r886058088">.mw-parser-output cite.citation{font-style:inherit}.mw-parser-output .citation q{quotes:"\"""\"""'""'"}.mw-parser-output .citation .cs1-lock-free In April 2011, a new collection of poetry, <i>She Walks In Beauty – A Woman's Journey Through Poems</i>, edited and introduced by Caroline Kennedy, was published. She launched the book at the John F Kennedy Library &amp; Museum at Columbia Point, Dorchester, MA.
</p>
